There isn't any \\"No\\", \\"not\\", \\"negative\\", or anything like that. Rather, they coyly announce, \\"We've minimized your discomfort.\\" When your child asks you if an immunization is going to hurt, what is your answer? Do you say, \\"No\\", or do you say, \\"Not much\\"? Note that here they don't say EITHER of those things. They say, \\"It's minimal.\\" That's a warning sign.<br /><br />Taking that into account, I set this bad boy onto my leg and nearly howled like Teen Wolf.<br /><br />This brings us to the Second Question.<br /><br />Is it efficient?<br /><br />This was possibly where I made my critical choice.   91. My name is Wandrwoman and I am a long term epilator. My introduction to this method of hair removal was sometime in the late 1980's with the Epilady, a medieval looking device with an exposed curved metal coil. The genius principal of the Epilady was that the metal coil would rotate and vibrate at a high speed and yank out your leg hair like an efficient electrical mower-tweezer.<br /><br />I have to admit that the leap of faith it took to use the Epilady for the first time was pretty intense. Just looking at the exposed vibrating and rotating coil was enough to send one running for the hills. But I was younger then and far more trusting. Dragging the Epilady along my bare shin stung more than hurt. All in all the experience was far less painful than childbirth and far less expensive than waxing.<br /><br />The most important point to remember about epilating is that the more you do it, the less you need it. Eventually, you need it very rarely. The hair is pulled out at the root. After each use the hair grows back finer and finer until it hardly grows back at all. At first, most women will use an epilator every few weeks. Then perhaps once a month. Eventually, it will be an occasional thing, more often than every leap year, but only when needed. I absolutely promise that the discomfort lessens with use.<br /><br />Epilators have come a long way baby, since the 1980's. The exposed coils have been replaced by a turning cylinder with tiny metal plates that open and close as they pass along the surface of your leg. My next epilator was the Braun Silk-Epil Super Soft which was faster and more accurate and could be used on parts of the body you would never want to place near an exposed rotating and vibrating coil.<br /><br />My brand new Braun Silk-Epil 5 is an enormous improvement over my old Braun. If you are thinking of upgrading, to do so is quite worthwhile.<br /><br />The Silk-Epil 5 now has 40 tweezer-plates on its rotating head, many more and more closely placed than earlier models. These tweezer-plates can remove fine hairs as short as 0.5mm. The rotating head also now pivots which better follows the contours of your body. I found the use was faster, more comfortable and fewer hairs were missed. The device now has a comfortable ergonomic shape that fits easily into your hand.<br /><br />Two different caps are supplied to be used with the epilating head. One cap has \\"High Frequency Massaging Rollers\\" that are supposed to \\"stimulate the skin effectively for an extra gentle epilation.\\" I found that this pivoting cap was extremely comfortable to use and that the rollers helped guide the hair towards the tweezer-plates. The other cap is called \\"the efficiency cap\\". It has no rollers but it pivots to \\"ensure maximal skin contact\\". I preferred the cap with the rollers as it was more comfortable and seemed to be more efficient.<br /><br />A razor head with a trimmer cap is also supplied with the Silk-Epil 5. The recommendation is to use the razor to trim longer hair to a length 2-5mm that is most suitable for epilating. This electric razor works well, but I would rather use the epilator. I suppose if you try and hate epilating, you at least have the razor to use.<br /><br />The Silk-Epil 5 has a tiny light on the bottom. I was extremely judgmental about this until I used the device and found that the light did helpfully illuminate the area I was working on.<br /><br />A \\"cooling glove\\" (a gel pack that fits into a plastic sleeve) is supplied. I didn't need to use it because I didn't have any discomfort or pain. My household can always use an extra gel pack, though, so it is sitting in the freezer waiting for the next ache or bruise.<br /><br />Another benefit of the Silk-Epil 5 is that, once you remove the electric cord, it is fully submersible in water for cleaning.<br /><br />Unfortunately, it can't be used in the shower or bath because it is not rechargeable. It must be attached to a power cord to be used. The chart on the Amazon product page outlining the various Braun Silk-Epil models says that the Silk-Epil 5 is rechargeable. This is inaccurate.<br /><br />The power cord is extremely long (90\\"), there is a small brush for cleaning the heads, and everything fits neatly into a draw string pouch for storage.<br /><br />This is a very good, well made product. I highly recommend it.azon product page outlining the various Braun Silk-Epil models says that the Silk-Epil 5 is rechargeable. This is inaccurate.<br /><br />The power cord is extremely long (90\\"), there is a small brush for cleaning the heads, and everything fits neatly into a draw string pouch for storage.<br /><br />This is a very good, well made product. I highly recommend it.

  192. I despise shaving and I knew the pain of waxing, but it wasn't the pain that scared me from buying an epilator. To be honest, it was the cost. I didn't want to buy a cheap one for the fear that, well, it would be a bad epilator. But I also didn't want to buy an expensive one, just in case it didn't live up to its performance. I didn't want to waste my money. Luckily, this product seemed a good in-between and it doesn't disappoint. I know people who've had their Brauns for three or four years and they're still going strong, so if mine lasts as much I'll be a happy woman.<br /><br />Yeah, the light and the trimming head are useful, but if we're honest I think the most worthwhile is the pivoting head feature. It's so easy to handle the epilator because of this. Some parts like the inside of the knee are still tricky because it's not a miracle worker, but it's what sold me on this. The cord is very long and it can be a bit of a bother sometimes, but you learn to work with it and I prefer it to having to recharge batteries. It barely misses hairs, unless you're going quickly over the area. If it does, usually going over it from another direction does the work. Some people say it can cut the hair, but I've looked at the hairs while cleaning (to make sure it was worth the pain, you know) and all the hairs I saw had their heads and such.<br /><br />Just keep in mind that, while you're doing it less frequently than shaving, this takes more time than shaving. The first time I epilated, I'd waited about three weeks for my hair to grow. Because it grows back at different rates and, efficiency, you know? Well, I used the trimming head first and, in the end, spent over two hours. From ankles to upper thigh, front and back. My legs were red for two days. A week later I saw some sporadic growth and epilated again, which took less than thirty minutes. Yesterday night, two weeks later from initial epilation, I had more growth all around. Not enough to be noticeable to other people, but enough for me. Again, it took me less than thirty minutes. The redness was a lot less in these occasions and was gone by the next morning.<br /><br />Four weeks of smooth skin is an overstatement. It could be true if you've spent years using epilators, I guess, but certainly not at the beginning. Expect something from 7-15 days, although it does depend for your climate. (Tropical summer for me, so hair grows faster.) This doesn't leave the skin completely smooth either, so I'd recommend exfoliating and moisturizing the day after, which you'll want to do once in a while to avoid a few ingrown hairs.

  224. I did not purchase this through Amazon but I am so happy with the purchase that I wanted to write a review. I have only used the epilator head so I cannot comment on the shaver and trimmer, or the cooling mitt. I am very pale with quite dark hair, and a little coarse. I use the product on my legs, arms, underarms, and entire bikini (Brazilian).<br /><br />PROS<br />1. It's easy to use - just plug into an outlet.<br />2. It's easy to clean - just remove the top, open, and run the head under warm water. It helps to twist the head while running it under warm water.<br />3. It has two speeds. The slower speed pulls hairs out at a slower speed, meaning that for any given area, it pulls fewer hairs out at a time and is therefore less painful than the higher speed would be. However, with the lower speed you will have to go over the area more times than with the higher speed. I like having the two speeds because it allows you to adjust based upon the sensitivity of the area you are epilating.<br />4. It has a light, which ended up being much more useful than expected and my favorite part of the product. It helps you see so many hairs that you would otherwise miss. I would definitely get an epilator with a light!<br />5. It pulls hairs out by the root. I do not see any hairs that were broken off. I have had minimal ingrown hairs.<br />6. The results are better than shaving and last much longer than shaving. I don't have a shadow immediately after shaving and I don't get hairy after a day or two. I can get away with epilating once a week, with a quick shave afterwards to get silky smooth.<br />7. I save money on razors because I can away with buying cheaper ones.<br /><br />CONS<br />1. It is not Wet/Dry.<br />2. It does not have the option of charging a battery or using batteries for travel use. It must plug into an outlet.<br />3. It is quite loud. It also sounds like an adult product, in my opinion.<br />4. It gets hot after awhile, usually after quite a long while but I did slightly burn myself when I tried using the product on my face and mistook the heat for the pain of epilating. I kept it on my upper lip for quite awhile, hence the burn, but otherwise it shouldn't be hot enough to burn you (unless you hold it on one spot for a long time like me!).<br />5. You don't get a baby smooth result. It's 99%. I still shave afterwards but I wouldn't have to if I didn't want to be super silky smooth, and it's just a quick shave.<br /><br />NEUTRAL<br />1. It takes longer to epilate than it does to shave but I have to epilate only once a week instead of shaving every other day. I am not spending any more time on hair removal now and I might be spending less.<br /><br />So, those are the pros and cons for the product itself. As for epilating itself: I was a first time epilator when I purchased this product. The first time I used the product, it was very painful. I do consider myself to have a low pain tolerance. I took Tylenol and used a topical lidocaine cream and I don't know if that helped at all. However, in one sitting, I managed to epilate my whole legs, my whole arms, including underarms, and my entire bikini area (Brazilian). I barely managed that last one. BUT, I have kept up with epilating and it has been much, much less painful after the first session. My legs, arms, and underarms are a breeze. The Brazilian still hurts a bit. Someone on Amazon recommended getting a wax first and then using the epilator for maintenance. I would highly, highly agree with her. You CAN do it my way, if you are broke like me, but it will hurt! If I could do it again, I would put a bag of ice in my lap while I epilated my legs and let the whole area numb up.<br /><br />As for ingrown hairs: I had a few after my first session. I did some research and changed a few things, and have not had any (or at least very many) ingrown hairs since.<br />1. Take a shower before you epilate.<br />2. Get a pair of exfoliating gloves to use in the shower. They're cheapand they work really well.<br />3. Clean the epilator head before and after each use with warm water AND rubbing alcohol. Don't forget to leave time for it to dry before using it.<br />4. Move from clean to dirty areas on your body. Do legs and arms first, and then underarms, and bikini area last.<br />5. Get a spray bottle and some witch hazel, and spray your body after epilating. If you can't shower before epilating, do this before epilating as well.<br />6. If you are going to do a quick shave after epilating, clean you razor before and after with rubbing alcohol, and spray yourself with witch hazel after shaving.<br /><br />Ta-da. It's super easy, not too painful after the first go, and you shouldn't have any ingrown hairs if you're careful (maybe bikini area but otherwise not). I would make this purchase again! And I am very picky.

  238. I began epilating last year with an [[ASIN:B003II4D2C Emjoi Divine]]. I chose the Emjoi because I wasn't sure if epilating was going to be my cup of tea and didn't want to spend a fortune to find out it wasn't. Over the past several months I've determined it's something I definitely want to stick with so I decided it was time to upgrade.<br /><br />My two biggest gripes with the Emjoi were the short battery life (I was replacing batteries every 30-45 minutes) and the curved shape of the tweezer head. The curved shape was nice when I was still learning the ins and outs of epilating as it's less prone to pinching but I was ready to move on to the big leagues with a flat epilator.<br /><br />This Braun model appealed to me because it is a corded model which meant I wouldn't be messing with swapping out batteries all the time, the tweezer head is flat, and it has an LED light which makes it easier to spot missed hairs. There were a few other perks about it (ie: the cooling glove and shaving attachment) that intrigued me as well. Overall my impression of the Braun 5-5280 Silk Epil Epilator is as follows:<br /><br />Pros:<br /><br />Corded design: Some people prefer cordless epilators but for me personally I prefer the corded design. I found the 7.5 foot long cord to be adequate for my needs and I don't find the cord to be bothersome or in the way at all.<br /><br />**IMPORTANT** The plug on this cord is designed to click into place inside the epilator but requires a firm push. I've noticed a few people complaining about the loose connector and thought this was important to point out. If your plug is falling out of your epilator it's because it's not properly clicked into place.<br /><br />LED light: As I mentioned previously I was interested in this feature but didn't have the highest of hopes as I knew it could be hit or miss. All I can say is WOW! It really makes a difference. When epilating I move through a small area, then move the epilator back a bit to shine the light on the area I just epilated. The LED light makes it very easy to spot any missed hairs. After seeing the difference I'll never go back to a non-lighted model.<br /><br />Tweezer accuracy: The 40 tweezers on this unit are very accurate at locating and plucking hairs. I've only experienced a few instances with this unit where it passed a hair more than once or twice without plucking it and the reason for this ended up being due to the head unit being full of plucked hairs (explained under cons). As long as the head unit is kept clear the unit does a remarkable job of plucking even the thinnest, shortest hairs.<br /><br />Cons:<br /><br />Hair build-up: The design of this epilator causes the plucked hairs to get caught and build up inside the rotating head unit. When this occurs the unit begins to lose accuracy. It's not difficult to open the head unit and brush away the excess hairs but is still an annoyance that's worth mentioning.<br /><br />Shaver head: I personally found the shaver head to be awful. It shaved maybe 50% of the hairs in a given area. Fortunately for me I did not buy this unit to use as a shaver so this isn't a deal breaker for me but is something to consider if you plan to use this attachment.<br /><br />Pinching: Make sure while epilating areas with skin that could potentially be pinched you're pulling your skin taut to avoid this. If it happens it's not the most horrible thing in the world but it does leave an unattractive red \\"hickey\\" where the skin was pinched and obviously doesn't feel very good.<br /><br />Other:<br /><br />SoftLift tips: I personally didn't notice anything special about the softlift tips cover over the standard efficiency cover. I find the efficiency cover easier to use as it's smooth so I just stick with that one.<br /><br />Design: I had my doubts about the tweezer design of this model. Instead of there being two moving metal tweezers that pinch together, this unit operates by having one moving metal tweezer press against a stationary plastic piece to pinch the hair. I had my doubts about this design but I can't consider it a complaint as this epilator blows my other epilator (with full metal tweezers) out of the water on accuracy and I didn't notice any significant hair breakage.<br /><br />Cooling glove: I can't list this as a pro or a con really as it did nothing for me. The most soothing thing you can do post-epilating is to apply a good natural lotion.<br /><br />Conclusion:<br /><br />Overall the Braun Series 5-5280 Silk Epil Epilator is a decent product. As I said it's not without its flaws but this seems to be par for the course when it comes to epilating and I didn't find the flaws to be significant enough to warrant deducting any stars from my rating. If you're looking for an epilator that is accurate, can be used for extended periods of time without having to worry about recharging/replacing batteries, and you don't mind being plugged into an outlet, I would definitely recommend this model.<br /><br />Epilating tips:<br /><br />Pain: epilating by its very nature causes discomfort but doesn't have to be unbearable. To minimize pain, hold your skin taut whenever possible and trim longer hair before epilating. Also I've found it to be less painful to epilate shortly after taking a hot bath or shower (make sure your skin is completely dry first!).<br /><br />Hair breakage: make sure you're using the appropriate speed for the hair you're trying to epilate. Personally I like to just stay on the slower speed as I find there to be a lot less breakage this way. Also make sure you're gliding slowly and giving the epilator plenty of time to pluck all the hairs in a given area.<br /><br />Post-epilating: Use a good natural lotion to help soothe your skin and prevent/minimize red bumps. Also, dry brushing regularly with a good natural bristle brush helps to both eliminate existing and prevent future ingrown hairs.st a stationary plastic piece to pinch the hair.   268. The last time I used an epilator was in the 80's when the Epilady first hit the market. My delight with the product was quickly extinguished the first time I used it and discovered how painful it was. I am embarassed to say it went back in the box and was pushed to the back of the closet, where it stayed. In the years since, I've been waxed and have had electrolysis and laser treatments, none of which were exactly comfortable.<br /><br />Hoping perhaps 25-30 years had brought some improvement in epilation, I tried the Braun Silk Epil Epilator 5-5280 on my legs. I won't tell you that it's not painful, but it doesn't hurt as much as I remember. If you've ever heard a commercial for laser hair removal, you may have noticed they tell you how quick it is, but they never mention that it hurts. The Braun Silk Epilator hurts, but you don't have the intense heat that I've experienced with five different types of lasers, which I find more uncomfortable, though quick. Electrolysis is great for small areas (such as eyebrows, upper lip, chin, etc), but would be prohibitive in terms of time and expense for larger areas but I don't think you could consider it for underarms or lower legs.<br /><br />Comparatively, the Epilator isn't quick - at least not for the legs. There are two settings - I and II, with I being \\"extra gentle\\" and II being \\"extra efficient\\" (read more painful). I find the I setting to be more tolerable, but it requires several passes to get all the hair in a given area. The light on this model is quite helpful. I have been using it on my legs and the hair doesn't seem to grow back as quickly as it does after shaving. However, it takes quite a while to epilate such a large area and though the pain isn't extreme, it gets hard to take to do both legs at the same time - and I am grateful I don't need to use it on the area they indicate are more sensitive - the bikini line and the underarms.<br /><br />This seems to be a nicely made little device and if you have the time, patience and can endure some discomfort, you will get decent results. When you consider the investment in time (going for the treatments) and finances required for waxing, electrolysis and laser hair removal treatments, epilation is the most efficient in both respects. All the alternatives to shaving require some degree of pain tolerance, but this is one that allows you to go at your own pace, at your convenience in the comfort and privacy of your home - and at a much lesser price. Particularly if you're on a budget, I would give this epilator a try before going for more costly methods.

Braun's epilators have proven reliable and durable for me over all of these years, and each one that I've gotten is STILL working, and going strong!<br /><br />The new line of shimmery white epilators that Braun has released, including this 5280, offer just about any new, or seasoned, epilator user all of the options that they'll want for as much hair removal as they're looking for. This 5280, with its three attachments, will get those new to epilation through to becoming seasoned epilator users without undue pain, and with years of reliable use.<br /><br />The epilator body is comfortable in the hand, and the buttons, and head release, are positioned where they are easy to reach while using the unit. The SmartLight is one of the best innovations Braun has come up with - that light reveals SO much more than one could previously see with these, especially around corners and in tighter spaces, that the epilator user is just about guaranteed to get every little hair.<br /><br /> There are others in this line that are wet/dry, and rechargeable, which is an advantage. Being able to epilate wet skin while actually in the shower adds a distinctive edge to successful epilation with a minimum of pain. Warm water makes the hair shaft open up, causing the shaft to release the hair more easily, so epilating either in the shower, or just post-shower, is going to be the best choice for the least painful experience. Over time, your hair WILL grow in finer, which can pose more of a challenge in getting the tweezers to grip the finer hair, but at that point, you might want to consider just epilating your skin when it's dry (something that was, once, an epilator user's only option...). Cleaning your epilator is easy enough; since many in this line can now be rinsed under running water, that's an option, but I still prefer to use the brush to remove any loose hairs, and follow that up with the application of a cotton ball soaked in rubbing alcohol, to clean and sterilize the tweezers on the heads.<br /><br />If you tend to have ingrown hairs, that CAN pose a problem with an epilator. I've had to back off of epilating more... sensitive, thicker-skinned areas, because epilation there has just prompted too many ingrowns for me, even with the daily use of a thick sugar scrub that I make up at home (all I use is a whole LOT of granulated white sugar, and just enough of any shower gel to make up a thick, foamy paste of sugar suspended in soap - kinda the consistency of creamed butter and sugar for cookie dough, ideally). There are other options (such as [[ASIN:B004OVH8H4 Emjoi After Epilation Cream With Hair Growth Inhibitor]], which I've never used), but for me, I think the smartest thing for me to do at this point is to stick to epilating areas where the hair will not grow back in curls that never break the surface of thicker skin...<br /><br />Overall, I'm happy with Braun's epilators, and I feel that their changes to their epilators have only added to their offerings, and made them that much more appealing to anyone looking to have hairless skin for many, many days at a time (about five for me, on average). It seems to me that either you're in the Emjoi camp, or the Braun camp, regarding epilators. I'm a happy user of Braun, and am willing to encourage anyone that's considering starting epilation to give this Braun epilator a try. I think you'll be happy with your choice, and that it'll last you for many, many years of happy hair removal! ; )that up with the application of a cotton ball soaked in rubbing alcohol, to clean and sterilize the tweezers on the heads.<br /><br />If you tend to have ingrown hairs, that CAN pose a problem with an epilator.   341. This is my first epilator, but I've been waxing and sugaring for several years and I generally prefer by-the-roots methods of hair removal to shaving. I was hoping I would be able to use it as my single, all-purpose method of hair removal.<br /><br />I didn't expect it to be cordless, based on the reviews here, and I'm fine with the long cord. Mine clicked in very securely and hasn't fallen out. I was prepared for the epilator to sound like a jet engine but it's quieter than a blender or hairdryer. The clipper attachment seems to be pretty much useless, which is not a big downside for me. The shaver seems okay but I doubt I'll use it. On to the specifics.<br /><br />LEGS \\"Removes hair as fine as a grain of sand\\" is probably overstating it, but it does as good a removal job on my lower legs as waxing did. There are some broken hairs left behind but waxing left some too. And the epilator is much, much easier to run frequently over my lower legs, so those broken-off hairs are sure to get yanked out sooner or later (especially since the epilator gets hairs shorter than waxing can). On my upper legs it is light years more convenient than waxing, particularly since I have (ahem) quite a lot of upper leg and thigh, and it used to take forever to wax a patch at a time.<br /><br />ARMPITS Frankly, unpleasant, but part of that is definitely my fault, since it was pretty shaggy there and didn't trim. I also got pinched once or twice before I realized just how important keeping the skin taut was. The second time I epilated my armpits was much better. Again, lots faster and less trouble than waxing.<br /><br />ARMS I actually never waxed these, mostly because I physically couldn't since I don't have 3 hands. I don't have a lot of hair on my arms and what there is is pretty fine, so I doubt I will epilate them regularly, but it was novel to try it once and the epilator did a great job. They were very red and bumpy for several hours after being epilated, no surprise there.<br /><br />BIKINI AREA Deeply unpleasant, but again, some of that was user error. Again with the shagginess that I was too impatient to trim, and I suggest you learn from my mistakes and trim the hair close to the skin, then let it grow for a week or so before epilating. There is no way around it, removing hair by the roots from the bikini area requires a lot of awkward contortion and reaching. The advantage of the epilator, of course, is that I don't have to do all those acrobatics with a dripping spatula of wax in one hand. It's easy to use with my nondominant hand, too. It is VERY important to keep the skin you're epilating as taut as possible, or the tweezers may nip you. So do small patches at a time, just as if you were waxing, with the skin held tight. The second time I epilated around the bikini line, it was much, much less unpleasant. The main disadvantage of the epilator is that it doesn't leave a very clean line, so if that's important to you, you'll have to tweeze, or edge with some waxing.<br /><br />PAIN Where waxing is usually one sharp, fast rip that has a sort of impact almost like being slapped, the epilator feels like a series of pricks or small zaps. Where you epilate, of course, affects how intense that sensation is. I don't mind the difference but some people might. The longer the hair is the more you will feel each individual hair being pulled and then yanked out.<br /><br />Overall, I find this to be well worth the minor downsides (moderate noise, cord, possible nips, sometimes more prolonged sensation of hair removal) because of the convenience it offers over waxing. Keeping up with hair removal is much, much easier when it doesn't involve a production.r />BIKINI AREA Deeply unpleasant, but again, some of that was user error.   358. I purchased this as a replacement for an older Braun model, the 5270 Xelle Silk-Epil Epilator. I'd had good experiences with the brand with the previous epilator and when it was damaged I figured I'd stick in house for a replacement. I've had it a little while now and it's still great.<br /><br />It may be that I am used to epilating by now, but I find this model to be markedly less painful than the previous or others I've tried. It's slightly more efficient and generally I don't have to make many passes to get rid of stubborn hairs. My one real qualm, and this is one I've had with other brands, is that it's actually pretty bad at getting those hairs &#34;as close as 0.5 mm.&#34; Rather than pluck them, the tweezers tend to break them because the hairs are too fine at that point to get a decent grip on. It's a minor quibble but since it's one of their big selling points, worth mentioning. I do a pass every other day with it as habit and regrowth lessens all the time.<br /><br />The real selling point though is the pivoting head. That thing is so useful, not just because it makes it easier to use on curved parts of the body but because it's SO MUCH EASIER TO CLEAN. You take the shield off the head and have access to the entire tweezer roller! No plucking little piles of hair out of the corners of the device, no shaking the thing repeatedly to get all the hairs out of the back. Open it up, shake or rinse it out and you're done.<br /><br />If you're new to epilating, I still recommend an Azulene Oil for aftercare (preferred Parissa as it is non-greasy and odorless), but your preferred aftercare will do. The legs do feel a little raw after an epilating session, sort of like a low-intensity rug burn. Don't try exfoliating your skin until a day later. Exfoliating and an aftercare product will help prevent ingrown hair.
